# Agent Gap Log

This is the working log for reducing agent-quality behavioral and heuristic gaps
between this repo's Rust terminal agent and:

- `/home/exedev/repos/codex`

The current goal supersedes the first feature-by-feature parity loop. The goal
is a subsystem-census-driven Codex agent-quality parity loop: every behavior
that can affect agent quality, model-visible context, tool-choice heuristics,
state/history reconstruction, retry/recovery, planning/collaboration,
finalization, verification, delegation, config/model metadata, or tool runtime
behavior must be inventoried, compared, fixed, or explicitly rejected with
evidence.

Browser interaction parity is intentionally out of scope for this loop and
should be handled by a separate goal. Approval/sandbox decision UI is also out
of scope unless a related behavior affects agent quality outside the approval
decision itself.

## Operating Loop

Every turn under this goal should:

1. Keep a full subsystem coverage matrix: Codex subsystem, Codex files, local
   files, model-visible effects, state effects, runtime effects, tests,
   Codex-auth comparison, status, and rationale.
2. Audit the open rows before implementation, using subagents when useful to
   cover multiple Codex subsystems in parallel.
3. Run a cheap Codex-auth smoke before continuing if provider/transport,
   request shaping, tool runtime, or subagent behavior could have regressed:
   one root `run-codex` prompt such as "What is the capital of France?", plus
   one spawned child `run-codex-session` that reads a tiny local file. If this
   fails, stop gap work and fix the smoke blocker first.
4. Select the largest coherent cluster of related heuristic gaps that can be
   fixed in the current turn without making evidence or verification unclear.
5. Compare this repo against Codex source behavior for every row in that
   cluster.
6. Record evidence for each gap or parity finding.
7. Decide whether to copy, adapt, defer, or intentionally reject each reference behavior.
8. Implement all aligned fixes in the selected cluster together.
9. Test implemented behavior against Codex using a subagent with Codex auth
   whenever the feature can be exercised through Codex behavior.
10. Run the narrowest useful local verification, plus the required full
   verification for TUI work.
11. Rerun the cheap Codex-auth root/subagent smoke after provider, request,
    runtime, or subagent changes.
12. Update this log and the human-facing overview, then state what remains
    open.

## Decision Rules

- Prefer batching related gaps when they share the same implementation surface,
  prompt behavior, runtime heuristic, or verification path.
- Do not artificially limit a turn to one small gap. If several related
  heuristics can be fixed safely and verified together, fix all of them in that
  loop.
- Avoid batching unrelated gaps if it would make evidence, review, or
  reference testing unclear.
- Copy Codex behavior when it affects agent quality, tool-use heuristics,
  persistence, planning, editing safety, verification behavior, or user-facing
  terminal behavior.
- Adapt only when this repo's Rust/TUI/browser wiring requires a different
  implementation shape while preserving the same observable behavior.
- Reject only when the behavior depends on product boundaries that must remain
  different in this repo. Rejections must include evidence and a reason.

## Required Reference-Test Gate

Feature work is not considered parity-tested until it has both:

- Local verification in this repo.
- A Codex-auth reference check performed by a subagent when the behavior can be
  exercised through Codex itself.
- A cheap Codex-auth health smoke for the current branch when the loop touches
  provider/transport, request shaping, tool runtime, or subagent behavior. The
  standard smoke is a direct root `run-codex` capital-of-France task and a
  spawned child `run-codex-session` that reads a tiny local file.

The reference check should record the prompt or workflow used, the observed
Codex behavior, the observed local behavior, and the resulting parity decision.
If a Codex-auth reference check is skipped, this log must record the exact
blocker.

## Subsystem Coverage Matrix

This matrix is the closure checklist for the current goal. Closed status in the
gap register requires evidence across every column, not just a passing local
test.

| G-034 | Context manager closure deltas | `crates/browser-use-core/src/lib.rs`, `crates/browser-use-protocol/src/lib.rs` | Interrupted-turn markers, contextual fragment classification, resume/fork context | `TurnContextItem`-like baseline payloads, response-item-backed checkpoints, rollback/resume/fork APIs, token replay, previous-response eligibility | Ten-scope Codex-auth audit, G-031/G-034 lifecycle subagent audits, Codex source audit for contextual fragments, and focused rollback/baseline/fork tests | Partial: local baselines now include a nested Codex-shaped `turn_context` payload for the represented cwd/date/timezone/network/model/personality/collaboration fields, `<turn_aborted>` remains contextual for rollback, assistant/tool-call/tool-output history can replay from persisted response items, compaction checkpoints keep `replacement_response_items`, checkpoint replay now prefers those response items, normal replay preserves unprojected API-history items instead of dropping them, normal and fork replay now count assistant inter-agent instruction envelopes as rollback turn boundaries, token totals for new `token_count` events preserve consumed usage like Codex, active-context token estimates are recomputed after represented compaction/rollback history rewrites, raw request normalization now matches Codex for missing local-shell/tool-search/function/custom outputs, orphan outputs, unsupported image parts, and unsupported image-generation results, OpenAI/Codex Responses providers now reuse previous responses only when the Codex-shaped prior-input plus response-item prefix and non-input request fields match, local compaction checkpoints now drop tool artifacts in favor of retained user turns plus a Codex-prefixed summary user message, and spawn forks now use filtered response-item history for `all`/`last_n` including exact local mailbox trigger/rollback boundaries for this event-store path. Full Codex context manager is not closed: exact resume reconstruction, broader `TurnContextItem` variants, remote/v2 compaction item handling, baseline clearing, exact typed token estimation/app-server replay surfaces, and public rollback/app-server APIs remain open. |

Remaining gaps: typed baseline coverage for collaboration/realtime/permission/filesystem/reference-context variants beyond local facts, exact reverse rollout reconstruction for resume, exact compaction baseline clearing, public rollback/resume/fork APIs with active-turn validation, interrupted fork snapshots, exact typed token estimation, and app-server token replay surfaces. |

Current addendum for the large matrix: the 2026-05-25 shutdown/config/transport
slice moved G-028, G-031, and G-032 forward. CLI/TUI shutdown now has the
whole-registry unified-exec cleanup guard; represented `allowed_web_search_modes`
constraints and hosted-tool request accounting are implemented; TTFT now starts
on first hosted/tool/raw response items; and inbound `response.processed` alone
is covered by an incomplete-stream regression. Remaining related work is the
true websocket client ack/fallback path, cloud/admin config-requirements
provenance, and any future app-server or alternate entry-point shutdown wiring.

Current addendum for G-028: the 2026-05-25 post-exit/cancel batch moved the
output-drain and stop-cleanup pieces forward. Local now has Codex-shaped 50 ms
post-exit reader drain, 100 ms background trailing-output grace, trailing
`command.output` before `command.finished`, descendant-pipe hang avoidance, and
core/CLI/TUI cancellation cleanup for the current agent subtree. Remaining
unified-exec work is narrower: pause-aware waits require a local pause signal,
here-doc prefix metadata is mostly approval/rule metadata, zsh-fork and deeper
non-Unix parser policy are still open, explicit reader cancellation internals
can be revisited if late detached readers become observable, and app-server or
alternate-entry shutdown wiring only matters if those surfaces are added.

Current addendum for the 2026-05-26 local-agent-quality batch: local now has
represented Codex-style goal tools (`get_goal`, `create_goal`, `update_goal`),
model-visible local skill inventory injection from `CODEX_HOME/skills`, CLI
`review` prompt entry points for uncommitted/base/commit/custom review shapes,
CLI `user-shell` context recording as model-visible workspace context,
successful `apply_patch` `turn.diff` sidecars, child follow-up replay of
spawn-time role config overrides, and shell command bootstrap from a bounded
per-thread shell snapshot. The local near-deadline synthetic warning was
removed so the model no longer receives a non-Codex budget heuristic. The
portable fallback prompt was expanded without Codex/OpenAI provider branding.
Follow-up fixes from the ten-subagent audit added per-goal token baselines and
single-goal-per-thread `create_goal` semantics, made `user-shell` run from the
session cwd with Codex-like command env defaults and truncated model-visible
history, materialized unambiguous plain `$SkillName` text mentions into
skill context, converted CLI `review` sessions into an isolated review mode
with review base instructions and disabled goal/multi-agent/web/image tools,
added `features.goals` gating for represented goal tools, added
`compact_prompt` / `compact_prompt_file` / `experimental_compact_prompt_file`
for local compaction summaries, records server model reroutes and unknown-model
catalog fallback warnings as startup/model sidecars, avoids advertising
unimplemented `prevent_idle_sleep`, validates/caps inline local images before
model replay, and changed plugin MCP wording so configured servers are not
presented as callable tools unless separately exposed. Verification: `cargo fmt --check`, `cargo test`, `uv run --with
pytest python -m pytest -q`, `git diff --check`, and two live Codex-auth
root/child smokes all passed. Remaining active non-browser gaps after this batch
are true websocket ack/fallback transport, dynamic MCP/app/deferred inventory
surfaces, hook runtime/context behavior, deeper goal continuation/budget
steering, exact shell snapshot edge parity across zsh/non-Unix shells, memory
read-path context, full image resizing parity beyond validation/capping, and
app-server lifecycle surfaces where they materially affect local agent quality.

Current addendum for the 2026-05-26 broad local-runtime batch: local now gates
the browser-harness prompt overlay on actual browser-mode runs, so non-browser
agent tasks receive the Codex terminal-agent prompt without browser tool
heuristics leaking into normal coding work. CLI and dataset browser runs still
set browser mode and keep the browser contract. Local compaction remains
portable/local-only, but CLI runs can now ask the active provider to produce the
handoff summary before falling back to deterministic local summarization. A
first non-approval hook runtime is implemented for command hooks:
`SessionStart`, `UserPromptSubmit`, `PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, assistant-text
`Stop`, `done`-tool `Stop`, and local `PreCompact`/`PostCompact` can add
model-visible developer hook context. `PreToolUse` can update tool input or
block a tool call, exit-code-2 blocks now match Codex's main PreToolUse,
UserPromptSubmit, and Stop semantics, async command hooks are skipped rather
than spawned out-of-band, and hook start/completion/failure/skipped events are
recorded. Approval UI semantics remain intentionally out of scope. Independent
read-only file/image tools now use the existing parallel dispatch path, parallel
`view_image` respects the active model's original-detail support, and unrelated
pre/post hooks no longer disable safe parallel batches. The turn loop records a
`git_worktree` `turn.diff` sidecar after tool execution so shell-originated file
changes are observable like patch-originated changes. External prompt/mailbox
drain now records `agent.turn_queue_drained`, making the active-turn input
queue visible for follow-up audits. CLI, dataset, and TUI runs enable local
model compaction. Focused local coverage was added for browser-prompt gating,
PreToolUse input update/context injection, PreToolUse exit-code blocking,
Pre/PostCompact hook execution, Stop-hook blocking on the `done` path,
provider-backed model compaction, and read-only parallel batch ordering.
Remaining active gaps after this batch: exact Codex hook regex/agent/prompt
handler parity, SubagentStart/SubagentStop hook integration, dynamic
MCP/app/tool inventory, websocket ack/fallback, app-server lifecycle/input-queue
protocol events, streaming-time tool scheduling, exact `TurnDiffTracker`
semantics, and deeper goal budget steering.

Follow-up audit summary from ten read-only subagents on 2026-05-26: the batch
did not close the agent-quality gap. The strongest repeated findings were
missing non-approval hook runtime (`SessionStart`, `UserPromptSubmit`,
`PreToolUse`, `PostToolUse`, `PreCompact`, `Stop`) before the broad
local-runtime batch; the current open hook work is exact matcher/handler
coverage, SubagentStart/SubagentStop integration, prompt/agent hook handlers,
and permission-request hooks if local later models approval.
Other repeated findings were remaining goal runtime
features beyond the represented tool state (automatic continuation, hidden
goal context, and budget steering), prompt-only review mode instead of Codex's
isolated reviewer workflow, MCP/dynamic/plugin discovery tools described but
not callable, thinner skill discovery/injection than Codex's
budgeted/config/plugin/repo skill system, and user-shell execution still lacking
streaming/cancellation even after cwd/env/history fixes. Novel findings from
the second audit batch: true websocket `response.processed` ack/sticky fallback,
local image processing/resizing/invalid-image placeholders, `prevent_idle_sleep`
advertising without a sleep inhibitor, unknown-model fallback warnings,
memory-read context injection, server-side model-reroute disclosure, and
configurable compact prompts.

## Closure Audit 2026-05-24

The 10-scope Codex-auth closure audit concluded that the gap is not closed.
Every audited area was either open or only partially closed:

- Prompt/context: aligned for current AGENTS/environment/base slices, still open
  for apps, skills, plugins, collaboration, realtime, permission/profile update
  surfaces, and full reference-context item semantics.
- Provider request/replay: main request fields, normal streaming Responses,
  failed/incomplete handling, reasoning usage, EOF error behavior, and
  output-schema text format are now partial/implemented; server metadata events,
  retry/fallback behavior, dynamic metadata, and lifecycle coupling remain open.
- Tool schemas: the direct v2 terminal tool surface is closed for the audited
  schema deltas. Remaining related work moved to deeper rows: dynamic model
  capability updates in G-032, v1/namespaced multi-agent behavior in G-033, and
  non-schema tool runtime semantics in G-028/G-029.
- Unified exec: env defaults, default login behavior, explicit-shell fallback,
  process id allocation/pruning, background completion events, final transcript
  events, no-newline partial-output streaming, write-error model text, and
  active truncation policy, cross-turn process lifetime after normal
  completion, represented Unix tree-sitter shell parsing, shell-specific argv,
  six-hex chunk ids, the stdin reaction window, bounded post-exit drain,
  trailing-output background finalization, and cancellation/stop cleanup are now
  partially aligned.
  Still open: optional zsh-fork behavior, deeper non-Unix shell policy/parser
  semantics beyond argv derivation, pause-aware waits, here-doc metadata,
  code-mode JSON, explicit reader cancellation internals if needed, and any
  future app-server/alternate-entry shutdown wiring.
- Patch: contextual hunk semantics, EOF semantics, pure-addition placement,
  freeform preverification, sequential runtime application, exact output
  newline behavior, streaming progress events, structured final lifecycle
  payloads, and committed-prefix tracking for runtime failures are now partially
  aligned. Still open: exact app-server patch notification surfaces, fuller
  streaming parser/throttle behavior, and sandbox-dependent path protections.
- Context manager: open for true `TurnContextItem` breadth, interrupted-turn
  markers, true fork/resume metadata, rollback boundaries, and token
  recomputation.
- Multi-agent: open for v1 tools, exact rollout forking, mailbox/input-queue
  semantics, full v2 config, dynamic model catalog propagation, and app-server
  bridge events.
- Config/model catalog: open for full `ConfigLayerStack`, thread/project layers,
  dynamic `ModelsManager`, typed `ModelMessages`, and harness-level base
  instruction overrides.
- Collaboration/Plan mode: partial for exact Default/Plan collaboration
  templates, config-gated injection, later-turn developer updates, Plan-mode
  `update_plan` rejection, default-mode runtime rejection for
  `request_user_input`, root-only Plan-mode `request_user_input`, always-visible
  collaboration tool specs, and final `<proposed_plan>` extraction. Still open:
  mode UI/API wiring, user-input answer UI, streaming plan deltas/rendering,
  full app-server collaboration events, and feature-flag/config breadth.
- Lifecycle/finalization: partial for Codex-shaped task lifecycle sidecars,
  hidden final-answer markup stripping, `end_turn=false`, `StreamError`,
  `TokenCount`, and the SSE `response.failed` requested-delay slice; still open
  for response-item rollout finalization, previous-response/websocket resume,
  transport fallback behavior, broader typed ApiError coverage, app-server
  notifications, and full compaction/token lifecycle.

## Open Questions

- Which Codex revision should be treated as the stable reference if the Codex
  repo moves during the experiment?
- What exact harness should be used for repeatable Codex-auth subagent tests:
  prompt transcript comparison, golden task suite, or both?
- When this harness grows an approval UI, should feature-enabled
  `additional_permissions` support be implemented before or alongside
  execpolicy prefix-rule approvals?

| 2026-05-26 | Added per-turn tool router substrate | `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test -q -p browser-use-core v1_multi_agent_tools_defer_behind_tool_search_when_supported_like_codex`; `cargo test -q -p browser-use-core shell_parallel_support_uses_visible_handler_capability_like_codex` | Focused tests passed / partial parity | Core now builds a Codex-shaped `ToolRouter` for each provider turn. The router owns the registry, model-visible tool specs, deferred BM25 `tool_search` index, search-source descriptions, visible handler lookup, parallel eligibility, streaming predispatch eligibility, and dispatch-time handler lookup. The provider turn, read-only streaming scheduler, parallel batches, serial dispatch, and `tool_search` now share that same router instead of independently rebuilding static registries. This closes the represented static-router inconsistency and creates the client-side substrate needed for future dynamic callable inventories. Remaining router gaps are actual MCP/app/plugin/extension callable contributors, provider-neutral dynamic tool executors, and Codex's full async tool future lifecycle with cancellation/read-write gating. |
